<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Sport of athletics</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Sports involving running, jumping, throwing and walking</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For the group of competitive sports and games requiring physical skill, see <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(physical_culture)" title="Athletics (physical culture)">Athletics (physical culture)</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Athletics_(disambiguation)" title="Athletics (disambiguation)">Athletics</a>.</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vcard"><caption class="infobox-title fn" style="padding-bottom:0.2em;">Athletics</caption><tbody><tr><td class="infobox-image" colspan="2"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Athletics_competitions.jpg"><img alt="Athletics competitions.jpg" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="2070" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Athletics_competitions.jpg/300px-Athletics_competitions.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Athletics_competitions.jpg/450px-Athletics_competitions.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Athletics_competitions.jpg/600px-Athletics_competitions.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em; padding-right:1.0em;">Highest <a href="/wiki/Sports_governing_body" title="Sports governing body">governing body</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/World_Athletics" title="World Athletics">World Athletics</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2" style="background:#eee;">Characteristics</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em; padding-right:1.0em;"><a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_sports" title="Mixed-sex sports">Mixed-sex</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Yes</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em; padding-right:1.0em;">Type</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Outdoor or indoor</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2" style="background:#eee;">Presence</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em; padding-right:1.0em;"><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Present since inaugural <a href="/wiki/1896_Summer_Olympics" title="1896 Summer Olympics">1896 Olympics</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="line-height:1.3em; padding-right:1.0em;"><a href="/wiki/Paralympic_Games" title="Paralympic Games">Paralympic</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">Present since inaugural <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Paralympics" title="1960 Summer Paralympics">1960 Paralympics</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Athletics</b> is a group of <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sporting</a> events that involves competitive <a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">running</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jumping" title="Jumping">jumping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Throwing_sports" title="Throwing sports">throwing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Walking" title="Walking">walking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The most common types of athletics competitions are <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Road_running" title="Road running">road running</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country running</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Racewalking" title="Racewalking">racewalking</a>.
</p><p>The results of <a href="/wiki/Racing" title="Racing">racing</a> events are decided by finishing position (or time, where measured), while the jumps and throws are won by the <a href="/wiki/Athlete" title="Athlete">athlete</a> that achieves the highest or furthest measurement from a series of attempts. The simplicity of the competitions, and the lack of a need for expensive equipment, makes athletics one of the most common types of sports in the world. Athletics is mostly an individual sport, with the exception of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relay_(athletics)" title="Relay (athletics)">relay races</a> and competitions which combine athletes' performances for a team score, such as cross country.
</p><p>Organized athletics are traced back to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Olympic_Games" title="Ancient Olympic Games">Ancient Olympic Games</a> from 776 BC. The rules and format of the modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_events" title="Athletics events">events in athletics</a> were defined in Western Europe and North America in the 19th and early 20th century, and were then spread to other parts of the world. Most modern top level meetings are held under the auspices of <a href="/wiki/World_Athletics" title="World Athletics">World Athletics</a>, the global governing body for the sport of athletics, or its member continental and national federations.
</p><p>The athletics meeting forms the backbone of the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympics</a>. The foremost international athletics meeting is the <a href="/wiki/World_Athletics_Championships" title="World Athletics Championships">World Athletics Championships</a>, which incorporates track and field, marathon running and race walking. Other top level competitions in athletics include the <a href="/wiki/World_Athletics_Cross_Country_Championships" title="World Athletics Cross Country Championships">World Athletics Cross Country Championships</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Half_Marathon_Championships" title="World Half Marathon Championships">World Half Marathon Championships</a>. Athletes with a <a href="/wiki/Physical_disability" title="Physical disability">physical disability</a> compete at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Paralympic_Games" title="Summer Paralympic Games">Summer Paralympics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Para_Athletics_Championships" title="World Para Athletics Championships">World Para Athletics Championships</a>.
</p><p>The word athletics is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">ἀθλητής</span></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc-Latn">athlētēs</i></span>, "combatant in public games") from <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">ἆθλον</span></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc-Latn">athlon</i></span>, "prize") or <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">ἆθλος</span></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc-Latn">athlos</i></span>, "competition").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Initially, the term described athletic contests in general – i.e. sporting competition based primarily on human physical feats. In the 19th century, the term athletics acquired a more narrow definition in Europe and came to describe sports involving competitive running, walking, jumping and throwing. This definition continues to be prominent in the United Kingdom and the former <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>.  Related words in <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a> also have a similar meaning.
</p><p>In much of North America, <i>athletics</i> is synonymous with sports in general, maintaining the historical usage of the term. The word "athletics" is rarely used to refer to the sport of athletics in this region. <i>Track and field</i> is preferred, and is used in the United States and Canada to refer to athletics events, including race-walking and marathon running (although cross country running is typically considered a separate sport).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sport_of_athletics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_physical_training_and_fitness" title="History of physical training and fitness">History of physical training and fitness</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sport_of_athletics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Discobulus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Discobulus.jpg/150px-Discobulus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Discobulus.jpg/225px-Discobulus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Discobulus.jpg/300px-Discobulus.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Discobulus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A copy of the Ancient Greek statue <i><a href="/wiki/Discobolus" title="Discobolus">Discobolus</a></i>, portraying a <a href="/wiki/Discus_throw" title="Discus throw">discus thrower</a></div></div></div>
<p>Athletic contests in running, walking, jumping and throwing are among the oldest of all sports and their roots are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric" title="Prehistoric">prehistoric</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Athletics events were depicted in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Egyptian" title="Ancient Egyptian">Ancient Egyptian</a> tombs in <a href="/wiki/Saqqara" title="Saqqara">Saqqara</a>, with illustrations of <a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">running</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heb_Sed_festival" title="Heb Sed festival">Heb Sed festival</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_jump" title="High jump">high jumping</a>  appearing in tombs from as early as of 2250 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tailteann_Games_(ancient)" title="Tailteann Games (ancient)">Tailteann Games</a> were an ancient <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> festival in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, founded circa 1800 BC, and the thirty-day meeting included <a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">running</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stone_put" title="Stone put">stone-throwing</a> among its sporting events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The original and only event at <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Olympic_Games" title="Ancient Olympic Games">the first Olympics</a> in 776 BC was a stadium-length <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Running_event" title="Running event">running event</a>  known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Stadion_(running_race)" title="Stadion (running race)">stadion</a></i>. This later expanded to include throwing and jumping events within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_pentathlon" title="Ancient pentathlon">ancient pentathlon</a>. Athletics competitions also took place at other <a href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Games" title="Panhellenic Games">Panhellenic Games</a>, which were founded later around 500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sport_of_athletics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cotswold_Olympic_Games" title="Cotswold Olympic Games">Cotswold Olympic Games</a>, a sports festival which emerged in 17th century <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, featured athletics in the form of <a href="/wiki/Sledgehammer" title="Sledgehammer">sledgehammer</a> throwing contests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Annually, from 1796 to 1798, L'Olympiade de la République was held in <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">revolutionary France</a>, and is an early forerunner to the modern Olympic Games. The premier event of this competition was a running event, but various ancient Greek disciplines were also on display. The 1796 Olympiade marked the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a> into the sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>Athletics competitions were held about 1812 at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_College,_Sandhurst" title="Royal Military College, Sandhurst">Royal Military College, Sandhurst</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ColbyWilliams1914_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ColbyWilliams1914-9">[9]</a></sup> and in 1840 in <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury" title="Shrewsbury">Shrewsbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shropshire" title="Shropshire">Shropshire</a> at the Royal <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_School" title="Shrewsbury School">Shrewsbury School</a> Hunt. The Royal Military Academy at Woolwich held an organised competition in 1849, and a regular series of closed meetings open only to undergraduates, was held by <a href="/wiki/Exeter_College,_Oxford" title="Exeter College, Oxford">Exeter College, Oxford</a>, from 1850.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The annual <a href="/wiki/Wenlock_Olympian_Games" title="Wenlock Olympian Games">Wenlock Olympian Games</a>, first held in 1850 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wenlock,_Shropshire" title="Wenlock, Shropshire">Wenlock</a>, England, incorporated athletics events into its sports programme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first modern-style indoor athletics meetings were recorded shortly after in the 1860s, including a meet at Ashburnham Hall in London which featured four running events and a triple jump competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amateur_Athletic_Association" title="Amateur Athletic Association">Amateur Athletic Association</a> (AAA) was established in England in 1880 as the first national body for the sport of athletics and began holding its own annual athletics competition – the <a href="/wiki/AAA_Championships" title="AAA Championships">AAA Championships</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> also began holding an annual national competition – the <a href="/wiki/USA_Outdoor_Track_and_Field_Championships" title="USA Outdoor Track and Field Championships">USA Outdoor Track and Field Championships</a> – first held in 1876 by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Athletic_Club" title="New York Athletic Club">New York Athletic Club</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Champs_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Champs-14">[14]</a></sup> Athletics became codified and standardized via the English AAA and other general sports organisations in the late 19th century, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amateur_Athletic_Union" title="Amateur Athletic Union">Amateur Athletic Union</a> (founded in the US in 1888) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_des_soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9s_fran%C3%A7aises_de_sports_athl%C3%A9tiques" title="Union des sociétés françaises de sports athlétiques">Union des sociétés françaises de sports athlétiques</a> (founded in France in 1889).
</p><p>An athletics competition was included in the first modern <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> in 1896 and it has been as one of the foremost competitions at the quadrennial <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> ever since. Originally for men only, the <a href="/wiki/1928_Summer_Olympics" title="1928 Summer Olympics">1928 Olympics</a> saw the introduction of women's events in the athletics programme. Athletics is part of the <a href="/wiki/Paralympic_Games" title="Paralympic Games">Paralympic Games</a> since the inaugural Games in <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Paralympics" title="1960 Summer Paralympics">1960</a>. Athletics has a very high-profile during major championships, especially the Olympics, but otherwise is less popular.
</p><p>An international governing body, the International Amateur Athletics Federation (IAAF), was founded in 1912. It enforced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amateur_sport" title="Amateur sport">amateur sport</a> status on competitions during much of the 20th century. Professional competition continued at a low level, becoming increasingly more common as the century progressed. The <a href="/wiki/International_Track_Association" title="International Track Association">International Track Association</a> briefly formed a professional track and field circuit in the United States in the 1970s. Athletes used their increasing status to push for remuneration and the IAAF responded with the <a href="/wiki/IAAF_Golden_Events" title="IAAF Golden Events">IAAF Golden Events</a> series and the establishment an outdoor <a href="/wiki/World_Athletics_Championships" title="World Athletics Championships">World Championships</a> in 1983, including track and field, racewalking and a marathon event. In modern times, athletes can receive money for racing, putting an end to the so-called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amateurism" title="Amateurism">amateurism</a>" that existed before. The global body updated the name to the International Association of Athletics Federations in 2001, moving away from its amateur origins,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> before taking on its current name <a href="/wiki/World_Athletics" title="World Athletics">World Athletics</a> in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Comité International Sports des Sourds had been formed by 1922, to govern international deaf sports, including athletics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACanada_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACanada-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first organized international competitions for athletes with a  <a href="/wiki/Physical_disability" title="Physical disability">physical disability</a> (not deaf) began in 1952, when the first international <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stoke_Mandeville_Games" title="Stoke Mandeville Games">Stoke Mandeville Games</a> were organized for World War II veterans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACanada_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-ACanada-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ipc_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ipc-18">[18]</a></sup> This only included athletes in a <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair" title="Wheelchair">wheelchair</a>. This inspired the first <a href="/wiki/Paralympic_Games" title="Paralympic Games">Paralympic Games</a>, held in 1960. Competitions would over time be expanded to include mainly athletes with <a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">amputation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_palsy" title="Cerebral palsy">cerebral palsy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visual_impairment" title="Visual impairment">visual impairment</a>, in addition to wheelchair events.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sport_of_athletics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_athletics_events" title="List of athletics events">List of athletics events</a></div>
<p>World Athletics, the sport's governing body, defines athletics in six disciplines: <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Road_running" title="Road running">road running</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_walking" title="Race walking">race walking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country running</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_running" title="Mountain running">mountain running</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trail_running" title="Trail running">trail running</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Mountain running was added in 2003 and trail running was added in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>All forms of athletics are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Individual_sports" title="Individual sports">individual sports</a> with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Relay_race" title="Relay race">relay races</a>. However, athletes' performances are often tallied together by country at international championships, and, in the case of cross country and road races, finishing positions or times of the top athletes from a team may be combined to declare a team victor.
</p><p>Several further forms of competitive running exist outside of the governance of World Athletics. The <a href="/wiki/International_Skyrunning_Federation" title="International Skyrunning Federation">International Skyrunning Federation</a> (ISF) governs high-altitude mountain running, defined as <a href="/wiki/Skyrunning" title="Skyrunning">skyrunning</a>, and is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/International_Climbing_and_Mountaineering_Federation" title="International Climbing and Mountaineering Federation">International Climbing and Mountaineering Federation</a> rather than World Athletics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Competitive <a href="/wiki/Stair_climbing" title="Stair climbing">stair climbing</a> events, usually hosted in <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscrapers</a>, has two common names: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertical_running" title="Vertical running">vertical running</a> (as described by the ISF) and <a href="/wiki/Tower_running" title="Tower running">tower running</a> (as described by the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Towerrunning_World_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Towerrunning World Association (page does not exist)">Towerrunning World Association</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Snowshoe_running" title="Snowshoe running">Snowshoe running</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">winter sport</a> governed by the <a href="/wiki/World_Snowshoe_Federation" title="World Snowshoe Federation">World Snowshoe Federation</a>, which is similarly to cross country running but has athletes wearing <a href="/wiki/Snowshoe" title="Snowshoe">snowshoes</a> to race over deep snow on an obstacle-free course.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Ultrarunners" title="International Association of Ultrarunners">International Association of Ultrarunners</a> organises <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultra_running" title="Ultra running">ultra running</a> as an affiliate of World Athletics, but these long-distance forms of competition fit within World Athletics disciplines, albeit with additional distance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_and_field">Track and field</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sport_of_athletics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Track and field">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">Track and field</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Track_and_field_stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2608" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Track_and_field_stadium.jpg/220px-Track_and_field_stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Track_and_field_stadium.jpg/330px-Track_and_field_stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Track_and_field_stadium.jpg/440px-Track_and_field_stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Track_and_field_stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical track and field stadium with an oval running track and a grassy inner field</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_(192)_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin,_3_September.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="729" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg/220px-100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg/330px-100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg/440px-100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_%28192%29_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin%2C_3_September.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:100_metres_race_winner_Sina_Schielke_(192)_and_the_other_Runners_-_ISTAF_2006_-_Berlin,_3_September.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International level women athletes at <a href="/wiki/ISTAF_Berlin" title="ISTAF Berlin">ISTAF Berlin</a>, 2006</div></div></div>
<p>Track and field competitions emerged in the late 19th century and were typically contested between athletes who were representing rival <a href="/wiki/Educational_institution" title="Educational institution">educational institutions</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_organisation" title="Military organisation">military organisations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports clubs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IAAFintro_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-IAAFintro-29">[29]</a></sup> Participating athletes may compete in one or more events, according to their specialities. Men and women compete separately. Track and field comes in both indoor and outdoor formats, with most indoor competitions occurring in <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a>, while outdoor events are mostly held in <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summer</a>. The sport is defined by the venue in which the competitions are held – the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_and_field_stadium" title="Track and field stadium">track and field stadium</a>.
</p><p>A variety of <a href="/wiki/Running" title="Running">running</a> events are held on the track which fall into three broad distance categories: <a href="/wiki/Sprint_(running)" title="Sprint (running)">sprints</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_distance_track_event" title="Middle distance track event">middle-distance</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long-distance_track_event" title="Long-distance track event">long-distance track events</a>. Relay races feature teams comprising four runners each, who must pass a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_(running)" title="Baton (running)">baton</a> to their teammate after a specified distance with the aim of being the first team to finish. <a href="/wiki/Hurdling" title="Hurdling">Hurdling</a> events and the <a href="/wiki/Steeplechase_(athletics)" title="Steeplechase (athletics)">steeplechase</a> are a variation upon the flat running theme in that athletes must clear obstacles on the track during the race. The field events come in two types – jumping and throwing competitions. In throwing events, athletes are measured by how far they hurl an implement, with the common events being the <a href="/wiki/Shot_put" title="Shot put">shot put</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discus_throw" title="Discus throw">discus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Javelin_throw" title="Javelin throw">javelin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hammer_throw" title="Hammer throw">hammer throw</a>. There are four common jumping events: the <a href="/wiki/Long_jump" title="Long jump">long jump</a> and <a href="/wiki/Triple_jump" title="Triple jump">triple jump</a> are contests measuring the horizontal distance an athlete can jump, while the <a href="/wiki/High_jump" title="High jump">high jump</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pole_vault" title="Pole vault">pole vault</a> are decided on the height achieved. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_events" title="Combined events">Combined events</a>, which include the <a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">decathlon</a> (typically competed by men) and <a href="/wiki/Heptathlon" title="Heptathlon">heptathlon</a> (typically competed by women), are competitions where athletes compete in a number of different track and field events, with each performance going toward a final points tally.
</p><p>The most prestigious track and field contests occur within athletics championships and athletics programmes at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-sport_events" title="Multi-sport events">multi-sport events</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Athletics at the Summer Olympics">Olympic athletics competition</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="World Championships in Athletics">World Championships in Athletics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_Summer_Paralympics" title="Athletics at the Summer Paralympics">Paralympic athletics competition</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Para_Athletics_Championships" title="World Para Athletics Championships">World Para Athletics Championships</a>, are the highest and most prestigious levels of competition in track and field. Track and field events have become the most prominent part of major athletics championships and many famous athletes within the sport of athletics come from this discipline. Discrete track and field competitions are found at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_championships" title="National championships">national championships</a>-level and also at annual, invitational <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Track_and_field_meet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Track and field meet (page does not exist)">track and field meets</a>. Meetings range from elite competitions – such as those in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IAAF_Diamond_League" title="IAAF Diamond League">IAAF Diamond League</a> series – to basic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_comers_track_meet" title="All comers track meet">all comers track meets</a>, inter-sports club meetings and schools events, which form the grassroots of track and field.
</p>
